make(chan chan struct{}),\n   318â†’\t\tcompress:    compress,\n   319â†’\t\tcEnc:        compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer(),\n   320â†’\t}\n   321â†’\tprefix := \"prometheus_tsdb_wal_\"\n   322â†’\tif filepath.Base(dir) == WblDirName {\n   323â†’\t\tprefix = \"prometheus_tsdb_out_of_order_wbl_\"\n   324â†’\t}\n   325â†’\tw.metrics = newWLMetrics(w, prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix(prefix, reg))\n   326â†’\n   327â†’\t_, last, err := Segments(w.Dir())\n   328â†’\tif err != nil {\n   329â†’\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"get segment range: %w\", err)\n   330â†’\t}\n   331â†’\n   332â†’\t// Index of the Segment we want to open and write to.\n   333â†’\twriteSegmentIndex := 0\n   334â†’\t// If some segments already exist create one with a higher index than the last segment.\n   335â†’\tif last != -1 {\n   336â†’\t\twriteSegmentIndex = last + 1\n   337â†’\t}\n   338â†’\n   339â†’\tsegment, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), writeSegmentIndex)\n   340â†’\tif err != nil {\n   341â†’\t\treturn nil, err\n   342â†’\t}\n   343â†’\n   344â†’\tif err := w.setSegment(segment); err != nil {\n   345â†’\t\treturn nil, err\n   346â†’\t}\n   347â†’\n   348â†’\tgo w.run()\n   349â†’\n   350â†’\treturn w, nil\n   351â†’}\n   352â†’\n   353â†’// Open an existing WAL.\n   354â†’func Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\n   355â†’\tif logger == nil {\n   356â†’\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n   357â†’\t}\n   358â†’\n   359â†’\tw := &WL{\n   360â†’\t\tdir:    dir,\n   361â†’\t\tlogger: logger,\n   362â†’\t}\n   363â†’\treturn w, nil\n   364â†’}\n   365â†’\n   366â†’// CompressionType returns if compression is enabled on this WAL.\n   367â†’func (w *WL) CompressionType() compression.Type {\n   368â†’\treturn w.compress\n   369â†’}\n   370â†’\n   371â†’// 377â†’\tw.WriteNotified = wn\n   378â†’}\n   379â†’\n   380â†’func (w *WL) run() {\n   381â†’Loop:\n   382â†’\tfor {\n   383â†’\t\tselect {\n   384â†’\t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n   385â†’\t\t\tf()\n   386â†’\t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n   387â†’\t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n   388â†’\t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n   389â†’\t\t\tbreak Loop\n   390â†’\t\t}\n   391â†’\t}\n   392â†’\t// Drain and process any discards all data after the corruption.\n   400â†’func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n   401â†’\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n   402â†’\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n   403â†’\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n   404â†’\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n   405â†’\t// a frequent concern.\n   406â†’\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n   407â†’\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n   408â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n   409â†’\t}\n   410â†’\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n   411â†’\t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n   412â†’\t}\n   413â†’\tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n   414â†’\t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n   415â†’\n   416â†’\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n   417â†’\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n   418â†’\tif err != nil {\n   419â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n   420â†’\t}\n   421â†’\tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n   422â†’\n   423â†’\tfor _, s := range segs {\n   424â†’\t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n   425â†’\t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n   426â†’\t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n   427â†’\t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n   428â†’\t\t\t// below.\n   429â†’\t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n   430â†’\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n   431â†’\t\t\t}\n   432â†’\t\t}\n   433â†’\t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n   434â†’\t\t\tcontinue\n   435â†’\t\t}\n   436â†’\t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n   437â†’\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n   438â†’\t\t}\n   439â†’\t}\n   440â†’\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n   441â†’\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n   442â†’\t// its records up to the corruption.\n   443â†’\tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n   444â†’\n   445â†’\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n   446â†’\ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n   447â†’\n   448â†’\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n   449â†’\t\treturn err\n   450â†’\t}\n   451â†’\t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n   452â†’\ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n   453â†’\tif err != nil {\n   454â†’\t\treturn err\n   455â†’\t}\n   456â†’\tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\n   457â†’\t\treturn err\n   458â†’\t}\n   459â†’\n   460â†’\tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\n   461â†’\tif err != nil {\n   462â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"open segment: %w\", err)\n   463â†’\t}\n   464â†’\tdefer f.Close()\n   465â†’\n   466â†’\tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\n   467â†’\n   468â†’\tfor r.Next() {\n   469â†’\t\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\n   470â†’\t\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\n   471â†’\t\t\tbreak\n   472â†’\t\t}\n   473â†’\t\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\n   474â†’\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"insert record: %w\", err)\n   475â†’\t\t}\n   476â†’\t}\n   477â†’\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\n   478â†’\n   479â†’\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\n   480â†’\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   481â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush page in repair: %w\", err)\n   482â†’\t}\n   483â†’\n   484â†’\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\n   485â†’\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\n   486â†’\t// are errors above.\n   487â†’\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\n   488â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close corrupted file: %w\", err)\n   489â†’\t}\n   490â†’\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\n   491â†’\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete corrupted segment: %w\", err)\n   492â†’\t}\n   493â†’\n   494â†’\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\n   495â†’\ts.Close()\n   496â†’\n   497â†’\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\n   498â†’\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\n   499â†’\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. err != nil {\n   538â†’\t\t\treturn 0, err\n   539â†’\t\t}\n   540â†’\t}\n   541â†’\tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\n   542â†’\tif err != nil {\n   543â†’\t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"create new segment file: %w\", err)\n   544â†’\t}\n   545â†’\tprev := w.segment\n   546â†’\tif err := w.setSegment(next); If no more records will fit into\n   581â†’// the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\n   582â†’// If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\n   583â†’func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\n   584â†’\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\n   585â†’\n   586â†’\tp := w.page\n   587â†’\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\n   588â†’\n   589â†’\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\n   590â†’\t// Enqueue and clear it.\n   591â†’\tif shouldClear {\n   592â†’\t\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\n   593â†’\t}\n   594â†’\n   595â†’\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\n   596â†’\tif err != nil {\n   597â†’\t\tp.flushed += n\n   598â†’\t\treturn err\n   599â†’\t}\n   600â†’\tp.flushed += n\n   601â†’\n   602â†’\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\n   603â†’\tif shouldClear {\n   604â†’\t\tp.reset()\n   605â†’\t\tw.donePages++\n   606â†’\t\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\n   607â†’\t}\n   608â†’\treturn nil\n   609â†’}\n   610â†’\n   611â†’// First Byte of header format:\n   612â†’//\n   613â†’//\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\n   614â†’const (\n   615â†’\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\n   616â†’\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\n   617â†’\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\n   618â†’)\n   619â†’\n   620â†’type recType uint8\n   621â†’\n   622â†’const (\n   623â†’\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\n   624â†’\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\n   625â†’\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\n   626â†’\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\n   627â†’\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\n   628â†’)\n   629â†’\n   630â†’func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\n   631â†’\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\n   632â†’}\n   633â†’\n   634â†’func (t recType) String() string {\n   635â†’\tswitch t {\n   636â†’\tcase recPageTerm:\n   637â†’\t\treturn \"zero\"\n   638â†’\tcase recFull:\n   639â†’\t\treturn \"full\"\n   640â†’\tcase recFirst:\n   641â†’\t\treturn \"first\"\n   642â†’\tcase recMiddle:\n   643â†’\t\treturn \"middle\"\n   644â†’\tcase recLast:\n   645â†’\t\treturn \"last\"\n   646â†’\tdefault:\n   647â†’\t\treturn \"<invalid>\"\n   648â†’\t}\n   649â†’}\n   650â†’\n   651â†’func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\n   652â†’\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\n   653â†’}\n   654â†’\n   655â†’// Log writes the records into the log.\n   656â†’// Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\n   657â†’func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\n   658â†’\tw.mtx.Lock()\n   659â†’\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n   660â†’\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\n   661â†’\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\n   662â†’\tfor i, r := range recs {\n   663â†’\t\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\n   664â†’\t\t\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\n   665â†’\t\t\treturn err\n   666â†’\t\t}\n   667â†’\t}\n   668â†’\treturn nil\n   669â†’}\n   670â†’\n   671â†’// log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\n   672â†’// - the final record of a batch\n   673â†’// - the record is bigger than the page size\n   674â†’// - the current page is full.\n   675â†’func (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\n   676â†’\t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\n   677â†’\t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\n   678â†’\tif w.page.full() {\n   679â†’\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n   680â†’\t\t\treturn err\n   681â†’\t\t}\n   682â†’\t}\n   683â†’\n   684â†’\t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\n   685â†’\tfinalCompression := w.compress\n   686â†’\tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\n   687â†’\tif err != nil {\n   688â†’\t\treturn err\n   689â†’\t}\n   690â†’\tif w.compress != compression.None {\n   691â†’\t\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\n   692â†’\n   693â†’\t\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\n   694â†’\t\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\n   695â†’\t\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\n   696â†’\t\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\n   697â†’\t\t\tenc = rec\n   698â†’\t\t\tfinalCompression = compression.None\n   699â†’\t\t\tsavedBytes = 0\n   700â†’\t\t}\n   701â†’\t\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\n   702â†’\t}\n   703â†’\n   704â†’\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\n   705â†’\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\n   706â†’\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\n   707â†’\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\n   708â†’\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\n   709â†’\n   710â†’\tif len(enc) > left {\n   711â†’\t\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); err != nil {\n   712â†’\t\t\treturn err\n   713â†’\t\t}\n   714â†’\t}\n   715â†’\n   716â†’\t// Populate as many pages as necessary to fit the record.\n   717â†’\t// Be careful to always do one pass to ensure we write zero-length records.\n   718â†’\tfor i := 0; The returned segment is ready for new appends.\nfunc OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n\tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\n\tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tstat, err := f.Stat()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tf.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\n\t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\n\t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\n\t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\n\t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\n\tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; It also ensures that torn writes never corrupt records\n// beyond the most recent segment.\ntype WL struct {\n\tdir         string\n\tlogger      *slog.Logger\n\tsegmentSize int\n\tmtx newWLMetrics(w *WL, r prometheus.Registerer) *wlMetrics {\n\treturn &wlMetrics{\n\t\tr: r,\n\t\tfsyncDuration: promauto.With(r).NewSummary(prometheus.SummaryOpts{\n\t\t\tName:       \"fsync_duration_seconds\",\n\t\t\tHelp:       \"Duration of write log fsync.\",\n\t\t\tObjectives: map[float64]float64{0.5: 0.05, 0.9: 0.01, 0.99: 0.001},\n\t\t}),\n\t\tpageFlushes: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"page_flushes_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of page flushes.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\tpageCompletions: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"completed_pages_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of completed pages.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\ttruncateFail: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"truncations_failed_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log truncations that failed.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\ttruncateTotal: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"truncations_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log truncations attempted.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\tcurrentSegment: promauto.With(r).NewGauge(prometheus.GaugeOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"segment_current\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Write log segment index that TSDB is currently writing to.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\twritesFailed: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"writes_failed_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of write log writes that failed.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\twalFileSize: promauto.With(r).NewGaugeFunc(prometheus.GaugeOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"storage_size_bytes\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Size of the write log directory.\",\n\t\t}, func() float64 {\n\t\t\tval, err := w.Size()\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"Failed to calculate size of \\\"wal\\\" dir\", \"err\", err.Error())\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn float64(val)\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordPartWrites: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_part_writes_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record parts written before flushing.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordPartBytes: promauto.With(r).NewCounter(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_parts_bytes_written_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of record part bytes written before flushing, including\" +\n\t\t\t\t\" CRC and compression headers.\",\n\t\t}),\n\t\trecordBytesSaved: promauto.With(r).NewCounterVec(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\t\tName: \"record_bytes_saved_total\",\n\t\t\tHelp: \"Total number of bytes saved by the optional record compression.\" +\n\t\t\t\t\" Use this metric to learn about the effectiveness compression.\",\n\t\t}, []string{\"compression\"}),\n\t}\n}\n\n// New returns a new WAL over the given directory.\nfunc New(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n\treturn NewSize(logger, reg, dir, DefaultSegmentSize, compress)\n}\n\n// NewSize returns a new write log over the given directory.\n// New segments are created with the specified size.\nfunc NewSize(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, segmentSize int, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n\tif segmentSize%pageSize != 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid segment size\")\n\t}\n\tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"create dir: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tif logger == nil {\n\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n\t}\n\n\tw := &WL{\n\t\tdir:         dir,\n\t\tlogger:      logger,\n\t\tsegmentSize: segmentSize,\n\t\tpage:        &page{},\n\t\tactorc:      make(chan func(), 100),\n\t\tstopc:       make(chan chan struct{}),\n\t\tcompress:    compress,\n\t\tcEnc:        compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer(),\n\t}\n\tprefix := \"prometheus_tsdb_wal_\"\n\tif filepath.Base(dir) == WblDirName {\n\t\tprefix = \"prometheus_tsdb_out_of_order_wbl_\"\n\t}\n\tw.metrics = newWLMetrics(w, prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix(prefix, reg))\n\n\t_, last, err := Segments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"get segment range: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Index of the Segment we want to open and write to.\n\twriteSegmentIndex := 0\n\t// If some segments already exist create one with a higher index than the last segment.\n\tif last != -1 {\n\t\twriteSegmentIndex = last + 1\n\t}\n\n\tsegment, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), writeSegmentIndex)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := w.setSegment(segment); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tgo w.run()\n\n\treturn w, nil\n}\n\n// Open an existing WAL.\nfunc Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\n\tif logger == nil {\n\t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n\t}\n\n\tw := &WL{\n\t\tdir:    dir,\n\t\tlogger: logger,\n\t}\n\treturn w, nil\n}\n\n// CompressionType returns if compression is enabled on this WAL.\nfunc (w *WL) CompressionType() compression.Type {\n\treturn w.compress\n}\n\n// Dir returns the directory of the WAL.\nfunc (w *WL) Dir() string {\n\treturn w.dir\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\n\tw.WriteNotified = wn\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) run() {\nLoop:\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n\t\t\tf()\n\t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n\t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n\t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n\t\t\tbreak Loop\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\n\tfor f := range w.actorc {\n\t\tf()\n\t}\n}\n\n// Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\n// It discards all data after the corruption.\nfunc (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n\t// a frequent concern.\n\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n\t}\n\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n\t}\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n\t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n\n\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n\n\tfor _, s := range segs {\n\t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n\t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n\t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n\t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n\t\t\t// below.\n\t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n\t// its records up to the corruption.\n\tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n\n\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n\ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n\n\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n\ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"open segment: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tdefer f.Close()\n\n\tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\n\n\tfor r.Next() {\n\t\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\n\t\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"insert record: %w\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\n\n\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\n\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush page in repair: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\n\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\n\t// are errors above.\n\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close corrupted file: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete corrupted segment: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\n\ts.Close()\n\n\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\n\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\n\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\n\ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn w.setSegment(s)\n}\n\n// SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\nfunc SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\n\treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\"%08d\", i))\n}\n\n// NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\treturn w.nextSegment(true)\n}\n\n// NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\treturn w.nextSegment(false)\n}\n\n// nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\n// It returns the file number of the new file.\nfunc (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\n\tif w.closed {\n\t\treturn 0, errors.New(\"wlog is closed\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\n\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn 0, err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"create new segment file: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tprev := w.segment\n\tif err := w.setSegment(next); err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, err\n\t}\n\n\t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\n\tf := func() {\n\t\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif async {\n\t\tw.actorc <- f\n\t} else {\n\t\tf()\n\t}\n\treturn next.Index(), nil\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\n\tw.segment = segment\n\n\t// Correctly initialize donePages.\n\tstat, err := segment.Stat()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\n\tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\n// the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\n// If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\nfunc (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\n\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\n\n\tp := w.page\n\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\n\n\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\n\t// Enqueue and clear it.\n\tif shouldClear {\n\t\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\n\t}\n\n\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tp.flushed += n\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tp.flushed += n\n\n\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\n\tif shouldClear {\n\t\tp.reset()\n\t\tw.donePages++\n\t\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// First Byte of header format:\n//\n//\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\nconst (\n\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\n\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\n\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\n)\n\ntype recType uint8\n\nconst (\n\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\n\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\n\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\n\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\n\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\n)\n\nfunc recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\n\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\n}\n\nfunc (t recType) String() string {\n\tswitch t {\n\tcase recPageTerm:\n\t\treturn \"zero\"\n\tcase recFull:\n\t\treturn \"full\"\n\tcase recFirst:\n\t\treturn \"first\"\n\tcase recMiddle:\n\t\treturn \"middle\"\n\tcase recLast:\n\t\treturn \"last\"\n\tdefault:\n\t\treturn \"<invalid>\"\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\n\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\n}\n\n// Log writes the records into the log.\n// Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\nfunc (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\n\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\n\tfor i, r := range recs {\n\t\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\n// - the final record of a batch\n// - the record is bigger than the page size\n// - the current page is full.\nfunc (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\n\t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\n\t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\n\tif w.page.full() {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\n\tfinalCompression := w.compress\n\tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif w.compress != compression.None {\n\t\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\n\n\t\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\n\t\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\n\t\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\n\t\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\n\t\t\tenc = rec\n\t\t\tfinalCompression = compression.None\n\t\t\tsavedBytes = 0\n\t\t}\n\t\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\n\t}\n\n\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\n\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\n\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\n\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\n\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\n\n\tif len(enc) > left {\n\t\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Populate as many pages as necessary to fit the record.\n\t// Be careful to always do one pass to ensure we write zero-length records.\n\tfor i := 0; i == 0 || len(enc) > 0; i++ {\n\t\tp := w.page\n\n\t\t// Find how much of the record we can fit into the page.\n\t\tvar (\n\t\t\tl    = min(len(enc), (pageSize-p.alloc)-recordHeaderSize)\n\t\t\tpart = enc[:l]\n\t\t\tbuf  = p.buf[p.alloc:]\n\t\t\ttyp  recType\n\t\t)\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase i == 0 && len(part) == len(enc):\n\t\t\ttyp = recFull\n\t\tcase len(part) == len(enc):\n\t\t\ttyp = recLast\n\t\tcase i == 0:\n\t\t\ttyp = recFirst\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\ttyp = recMiddle\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif finalCompression != compression.None {\n\t\t\tswitch finalCompression {\n\t\t\tcase compression.Snappy:\n\t\t\t\ttyp |= snappyMask\n\t\t\tcase compression.Zstd:\n\t\t\t\ttyp |= zstdMask\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported compression type: %v\", finalCompression)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tbuf[0] = byte(typ)\n\t\tcrc := crc32.Checksum(part, castagnoliTable)\n\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint16(buf[1:], uint16(len(part)))\n\t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint32(buf[3:], crc)\n\n\t\tcopy(buf[recordHeaderSize:], part)\n\t\tp.alloc += len(part) + recordHeaderSize\n\n\t\tw.metrics.recordPartWrites.Inc()\n\t\tw.metrics.recordPartBytes.Add(float64(len(part) + recordHeaderSize))\n\n\t\tif w.page.full() {\n\t\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t// TODO When the flushing fails at this point and the record has not been\n\t\t\t\t// fully written to the buffer, we end up with a corrupted WAL because some part of the\n\t\t\t\t// record have been written to the buffer, while the rest of the record will be discarded.\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tenc = enc[l:]\n\t}\n\n\t// If it's the final record of the batch and the page is not empty, flush it.\n\tif final && w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(false); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// LastSegmentAndOffset returns the last segment number of the WAL\n// and the offset in that file upto which the segment has been filled.\nfunc (w *WL) LastSegmentAndOffset() (seg, offset int, err error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\n\t_, seg, err = Segments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn seg, offset, err\n\t}\n\n\toffset = (w.donePages * pageSize) + w.page.alloc\n\n\treturn seg, offset, err\n}\n\n// Truncate drops all segments before i.\nfunc (w *WL) Truncate(i int) (err error) {\n\tw.metrics.truncateTotal.Inc()\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tw.metrics.truncateFail.Inc()\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\trefs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tfor _, r := range refs {\n\t\tif r.index >= i {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err = os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), r.name)); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (w *WL) fsync(f *Segment) error {\n\tstart := time.Now()\n\terr := f.Sync()\n\tw.metrics.fsyncDuration.Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())\n\treturn err\n}\n\n// Sync forces a file sync on the current write log segment. This function is meant\n// to be used only on tests due to different behaviour on Operating Systems\n// like windows and linux.\nfunc (w *WL) Sync() error {\n\treturn w.fsync(w.segment)\n}\n\n// Close flushes all writes and closes active segment.\nfunc (w *WL) Close() (err error) {\n\tw.mtx.Lock()\n\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n\n\tif w.closed {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"wlog already closed\")\n\t}\n\n\tif w.segment == nil {\n\t\tw.closed = true\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\t// Flush the last page and zero out all its remaining size.\n\t// We must not flush an empty page as it would falsely signal\n\t// the segment is done if we start writing to it again after opening.\n\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tdonec := make(chan struct{})\n\tw.stopc <- donec\n\t<-donec\n\n\tif err = w.fsync(w.segment); err != nil {\n\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tw.metrics.Unregister()\n\tw.closed = true\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Segments returns the range [first, n] of currently existing segments.\n// If no segments are found, first and n are -1.\nfunc Segments(wlDir string) (first, last int, err error) {\n\trefs, err := listSegments(wlDir)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn 0, 0, err\n\t}\n\tif len(refs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn -1, -1, nil\n\t}\n\treturn refs[0].index, refs[len(refs)-1].index, nil\n}\n\ntype segmentRef struct {\n\tname  string\n\tindex int\n}\n\nfunc listSegments(dir string) (refs []segmentRef, err error) {\n\tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tfor _, f := range files {\n\t\tfn := f.Name()\n\t\tk, err := strconv.Atoi(fn)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\trefs = append(refs, segmentRef{name: fn, index: k})\n\t}\n\tslices.SortFunc(refs, func(a, b segmentRef) int {\n\t\treturn a.index - b.index\n\t})\n\tfor i := 0; We have to be careful not to increment curr too\n// early, as it is used by Reader.Err() to tell Repair which segment is corrupt.\n// As such we pad the end of non-page align segments with zeros.\ntype segmentBufReader struct {\n\tbuf  *bufio.Reader\n\tsegs []*Segment\n\tcur  int // Index into segs.\n\toff  int // Offset of read data into current segment.\n}\n\nfunc NewSegmentBufReader(segs ...*Segment) io.ReadCloser {\n\tif len(segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn &segmentBufReader{}\n\t}\n\n\treturn &segmentBufReader{\n\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n\t\tsegs: segs,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc NewSegmentBufReaderWithOffset(offset int, segs ...*Segment) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\n\tif offset == 0 || len(segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\n\t}\n\n\tsbr := &segmentBufReader{\n\t\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\n\t\tsegs: segs,\n\t}\n\tvar err error\n\tif offset > 0 {\n\t\t_, err = sbr.buf.Discard(offset)\n\t}\n\treturn sbr, err\n}\n\nfunc (r *segmentBufReader) Close() (err error) {\n\tfor _, s := range r.segs {\n\t\tif e := s.Close(); e != nil {\n\t\t\terr = e\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn err\n}\n\n// Read implements io.Reader.\nfunc (r *segmentBufReader) Read(b []byte) (n int, err error) {\n\tif len(r.segs) == 0 {\n\t\treturn 0, io.EOF\n\t}\n\n\tn, err = r.buf.Read(b)\n\tr.off += n\n\n\t// If we succeeded, or hit a non-EOF, we can stop.\n\tif err == nil || !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {\n\t\treturn n, err\n\t}\n\n\t// We hit EOF; fake out zero padding at the end of short segments, so we\n\t// don't increment curr too early and report the wrong segment as corrupt.\n\tif r.off%pageSize != 0 {\n\t\ti := 0\n\t\tfor ; n+i < len(b) && (r.off+i)%pageSize != 0; i++ {\n\t\t\tb[n+i] = 0\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Return early, even if we didn't fill b.\n\t\tr.off += i\n\t\treturn n + i, nil\n\t}\n\n\t// There is no more deta left in the curr segment and there are no more\n\t// segments left.  Return EOF.\n\tif r.cur+1 >= len(r.segs) {\n\t\treturn n, io.EOF\n\t}\n\n\t// Move to next segment.\n\tr.cur++\n\tr.off = 0\n\tr.buf.Reset(r.segs[r.cur])\n\treturn n, nil\n}\n\n// Size computes the size of the write log.\n// We do this by adding the sizes of all the files under the WAL dir.\nfunc (w *WL) Size() (int64, error) {\n\treturn fileutil.DirSize(w.Dir())\n}\n","numLines":1049,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1049}}}

err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif err := cp.Close(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"close checkpoint: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Sync temporary directory before rename.\n\tdf, err := fileutil.OpenDir(cpdirtmp)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"open temporary checkpoint directory: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\tif err := df.Sync(); err != nil {\n\t\tdf.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, The WAL system implements:\\n\\n**WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)**:\\n- `CreateSegment(dir, k)` and `OpenWriteSegment()` create and open new WAL segment files\\n- `NextSegment()` and `nextSegment()` manage segment rotation when current segment reaches size limits (128MB default)\\n- `Segment` struct represents individual WAL segment files with read/write capabilities\\n- `WL` (WriteLog) struct is the main WAL implementation managing active segments, page buffering (32KB pages), and asynchronous operations\\n\\n**Record Logging and Encoding (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go and tsdb/record/record.go)**:\\n- `Log()` function batches records into pages with CRC32 checksums and optional compression (Snappy/Zstd)\\n- `Encoder` type provides methods to encode series, samples, histogram samples, tombstones, metadata, and exemplars\\n- `Decoder` type reads and decodes these record types from the WAL\\n- Records are split across page boundaries (7-byte headers with record type, length, and CRC)\\n- Record types: `Series`, `Samples`, `Tombstones`, `HistogramSamples`, `FloatHistogramSamples`, `Metadata`, `Exemplars`, `MmapMarkers`\\n\\n**WAL Repair on Corruption (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)**:\\n- `Repair()` function detects and handles WAL corruption by:\\n  - Identifying the corrupted segment and offset via `CorruptionErr`\\n  - Deleting all segments after the corruption point\\n  - Truncating the corrupted segment and re-inserting valid records up to the corruption point\\n  - Using `NewReader()` from `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` to parse existing records safely\\n\\n**Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)**:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function compacts WAL segments [from, to] into checkpoint directories\\n- Includes the most recent checkpoint and filters data based on:\\n  - `keep` function for series filtering\\n  - `mint` timestamp for dropping old samples/tombstones/exemplars/metadata\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint to enable incremental checkpoints\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` and `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` manage checkpoint cleanup\\n- Checkpoints are stored in segmented WAL format in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories\\n\\n**WAL Reading and Replay**:\\n- `Reader` in `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` reads records with CRC validation and decompression\\n- `LiveReader` in `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` reads actively-written WAL segments\\n- `Watcher` in `tsdb/wlog/watcher.go` monitors WAL for new data and processes via `WriteTo` interface\\n- `loadWAL()` in `tsdb/head_wal.go` replays WAL data during head block initialization\\n\\n**Page and Segment Format**:\\n- Records are written to 32KB pages within segments\\n- Record header format: 1 byte (type + compression flags) + 2 bytes (length) + 4 bytes (CRC32)\\n- Record types support fragmentation: `recFull`, `recFirst`, `recMiddle`, `recLast`, `recPageTerm`\\n- Torn page detection fills incomplete pages with zeros\\n- Segments are never rotated mid-record, ensuring atomicity at segment boundaries\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1097,"cache_read_input_tokens":61962,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1097},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7cf65e18-2ea6-4346-8023-5fafa10bf781","uuid":"a448e4dd-f6ca-4793-b9f8-e454ad2e96c3"}

The WAL system implements:\\n\\n**WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)**:\\n- `CreateSegment(dir, k)` and `OpenWriteSegment()` create and open new WAL segment files\\n- `NextSegment()` and `nextSegment()` manage segment rotation when current segment reaches size limits (128MB default)\\n- `Segment` struct represents individual WAL segment files with read/write capabilities\\n- `WL` (WriteLog) struct is the main WAL implementation managing active segments, page buffering (32KB pages), and asynchronous operations\\n\\n**Record Logging and Encoding (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go and tsdb/record/record.go)**:\\n- `Log()` function batches records into pages with CRC32 checksums and optional compression (Snappy/Zstd)\\n- `Encoder` type provides methods to encode series, samples, histogram samples, tombstones, metadata, and exemplars\\n- `Decoder` type reads and decodes these record types from the WAL\\n- Records are split across page boundaries (7-byte headers with record type, length, and CRC)\\n- Record types: `Series`, `Samples`, `Tombstones`, `HistogramSamples`, `FloatHistogramSamples`, `Metadata`, `Exemplars`, `MmapMarkers`\\n\\n**WAL Repair on Corruption (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)**:\\n- `Repair()` function detects and handles WAL corruption by:\\n  - Identifying the corrupted segment and offset via `CorruptionErr`\\n  - Deleting all segments after the corruption point\\n  - Truncating the corrupted segment and re-inserting valid records up to the corruption point\\n  - Using `NewReader()` from `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` to parse existing records safely\\n\\n**Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)**:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function compacts WAL segments [from, to] into checkpoint directories\\n- Includes the most recent checkpoint and filters data based on:\\n  - `keep` function for series filtering\\n  - `mint` timestamp for dropping old samples/tombstones/exemplars/metadata\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint to enable incremental checkpoints\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` and `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` manage checkpoint cleanup\\n- Checkpoints are stored in segmented WAL format in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories\\n\\n**WAL Reading and Replay**:\\n- `Reader` in `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` reads records with CRC validation and decompression\\n- `LiveReader` in `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` reads actively-written WAL segments\\n- `Watcher` in `tsdb/wlog/watcher.go` monitors WAL for new data and processes via `WriteTo` interface\\n- `loadWAL()` in `tsdb/head_wal.go` replays WAL data during head block initialization\\n\\n**Page and Segment Format**:\\n- Records are written to 32KB pages within segments\\n- Record header format: 1 byte (type + compression flags) + 2 bytes (length) + 4 bytes (CRC32)\\n- Record types support fragmentation: `recFull`, `recFirst`, `recMiddle`, `recLast`, `recPageTerm`\\n- Torn page detection fills incomplete pages with zeros\\n- Segments are never rotated mid-record, ensuring atomicity at segment boundaries\"\n}\n","numLines":70,"startLine":1,"totalLines":70}}}
